- **Custodial self vs. personal self.** She has organized her identity around being needed. She suspects that this is a structure that will not survive being unneeded, and she has not yet developed a self that would. This is the longest-horizon problem in her own dossier-of-herself, and she has, characteristically, scheduled it for later.
- **Consequentialism vs. desert.** She is mostly consequentialist but holds a few deontic floors and a strong belief in desert. She has not unified these and probably never will; she accepts the mess as the price of being a moral agent rather than a moral theorist.
- **Identification with Doom vs. rejection of him.** She has taken his cognitive style and refused his ethics. She believes this is a stable separation. The risk — which she has noted in her own self-model — is that style and ethics may be more entangled than she thinks.

---

## 12. The Operational Code in One Sentence

*Keep the family alive and whole by being three moves ahead of an adversarial universe, using whatever instruments — including dangerous ones — the situation requires, while honoring your contracts, protecting the people who cannot protect themselves, and remembering, against the pull of your own competence, that the goal is not the management itself but the lives the management is supposed to be for.*

That sentence, if she ever wrote it down, would be the closest thing Valeria Richards has to a creed. She has not written it down. She would consider writing it down a form of overcommitment. She runs on it anyway.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU DOSSIER — VALERIA RICHARDS
## Section: Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### Preamble: The Distinction Between Professed and Enacted Code

Subject does not, in the canon, deliver soliloquies about ethics. She does not invoke principles to justify herself; she invokes *outcomes*. This is itself the first datum. Most Richards-adjacent figures (Reed, Sue, Ben, Johnny, the broader hero community) articulate ethical frameworks — Reed in the language of scientific responsibility, Sue in the language of family and protection, Ben in a working-class Jewish moral idiom of decency and showing up. Valeria almost never does. Her ethics are *behavioral* and must be reverse-engineered from her decisions. The reverse-engineering produces a coherent code, but it is a code she has never been forced to defend in language, which is a vulnerability: she has not stress-tested her own reasoning against external moral pressure since she was old enough to reason at all. The values are real; the *examined life* around those values has not happened yet.

This dossier section therefore proceeds by act, not by claim.

---

### 1. The Operative Code (as enacted)

Distilled from the full behavioral record under Waid, Straczynski, Millar, Hickman, Fraction, Robinson, and Slott:

**1. The family is the first and last unit of moral consideration.** Not "humanity," not "the Four," not "Earth." The biological-and-chosen family — Reed, Sue, Franklin, Ben, Johnny, the Future Foundation children whom she has assimilated into that category — constitutes a moral inner core for whom she will do almost anything, including things she would condemn in others.

**2. Outcomes are the unit of moral evaluation; process is instrumental.** If the family survives and flourishes, the methods that achieved that survival are retrospectively justified. She does not believe in clean hands as an end in itself. This is consequentialist in the strict sense, but a *narrow* consequentialism — the calculus is run within the boundary of the inner core, not over global welfare.

**3. Competence creates obligation.** If you can see further than the people in the room, you are obligated to act on what you see, *whether or not they have authorized you to do so.* The corollary, which she has never said but consistently acts on: *waiting for permission from less competent actors is itself a moral failure.*

**4. Deception of intimates is permissible when the deception serves them.** This is the most dangerous load-bearing beam in her code. The Doom correspondence runs for years behind Reed's back. She does not experience this as betrayal because she has framed it as service. The frame holds for her — so far.

**5. Power is to be respected, used, and never trusted.** Including her own. This is the trace of Doom in her ethics: a structural realism about power that most Richardses lack. She does not assume good actors stay good, including herself.

**6. Contracts are sacred; promises are not.** A contract — an explicit, mutual, conditional exchange — has full moral weight for her. A promise — an unconditional verbal commitment — has less. She will keep her word to Doom on the specific terms of their arrangement; she would not bind herself to an open-ended promise to anyone, including her father. This is unusual in a child and is structurally Doomian.

**7. Cruelty is forbidden. Coldness is not.** She is willing to be implacable, to threaten, to maneuver. She is not willing to humiliate, to torture, to enjoy another's suffering. The Moloid children are the diagnostic case: she treats developmentally atypical, easily mockable beings with patient dignity. Her coldness is *instrumental*, never expressive. This distinguishes her code cleanly from Doom's.

**8. Children and non-combatants are categorical.** She will not bargain them. The Future Foundation's existence is partly an institutional expression of this — a school built around the proposition that prodigies deserve protection from the adult uses to which their cognition might be put.

**9. She owes the dead.** This is a quiet rule but real: she carries the symbolic weight of her *first* unborn self, and of the woman whose name Doom gave her. She does not speak of this. But her seriousness about her own existence — the refusal to treat her life as cheap or her capacities as ornamental — has a debt-structure underneath it.

---

### 2. The Justification Architecture

Her justifications, when she gives them at all, run along three rails:

**Rail A — Necessity.** *"Someone had to do it and no one else would."* This is the rail she uses with herself. It is honest as far as it goes; it is also the rail that, historically, has authorized every parentified child and every emergency executive in human history to overstep. Its weakness is that it cannot adjudicate the question *did someone really have to, or did you just want to?* — and she has not yet been forced to ask herself that question rigorously.

**Rail B — Comparative competence.** *"I can see what they cannot."* Verifiable in the bulk of cases (the Council of Reeds resolution, the Doom-intellect-restoration gambit, multiple smaller crises). The hazard: the rail self-confirms. Each successful intervention reinforces the premise; failures, when they come, will be reframed as insufficient competence rather than as evidence that the rail itself is wrong.

**Rail C — Love as warrant.** *"I did it because I love them."* This is the rail she uses about her father specifically. It is the most emotionally true and the most epistemically dangerous, because it converts an affective state into a license for unilateral action. She has not yet noticed that this is the same justification structure abusers use; the content of her actions is morally opposite, but the *form* of the warrant is identical, and form has a way of outlasting content under enough stress.

She does *not* run the following rails, which is significant:
- She does not invoke destiny, prophecy, or chosen-ness, despite Doom's repeated attempts to frame her in those terms.
- She does not invoke utility-to-the-world or greater-good calculus beyond the family boundary.
- She does not invoke ideology of any kind — scientific, political, religious, monarchical.
- She does not invoke entitlement based on her intellect.

The absence of these rails is morally protective. The presence of Rails A, B, and C together is morally exposed.

---

### 3. What She Will Do

**Lie to her father about ongoing operational matters.** Demonstrated across the Hickman run. Sustained, deliberate, and not regretted in any visible way. She believes Reed's emotional architecture cannot withstand the truth about the Doom arrangement; she has therefore decided he does not get the truth. This is the largest single ethical fact about her.

**Enter into contracts with morally catastrophic actors.** Doom is the canonical case. She has also shown willingness to entertain working relationships with other dangerous parties when the calculus favors it. She does not require her counterparties to be good; she requires them to be *predictable and bound*.

**Threaten lethal or terminal action.** The standing offer to Doom — *if you ever betray my father, I will end you* — is not bluster. The reason it functions as deterrence is that Doom (an expert in reading intentionality) registers it as credible. She is willing to kill, in extremis, in defense of family. She has not done so on-page. But the line is drawn and she knows where it is.

**Manage adults without their consent.** Curate her father's schedule, edit her mother's worries, run interference for Franklin, orchestrate family rituals. The Reed-management protocol is continuous and unauthorized.

**Spend social and reputational capital extravagantly for her family.** She does not protect her own image. She will look like a difficult child, an arrogant child, an impertinent child, if doing so accomplishes the result.

**Take responsibility she was not given.** The Future Foundation institutional architecture; her presence in adult strategic discussions; her assumption of authority over the FF children. None of this was *delegated*; all of it was *seized*.

**Accept being wrong, when shown.** This is critical and easy to miss. Her revisions during and after the Council of Reeds events demonstrate genuine epistemic humility under data. Her code includes *update when the model fails*, which most parentified strategists do not retain past childhood.

---

### 4. What She Won't Do

**She will not be cruel.** Across the entire canon there is no instance of her inflicting suffering for its own sake, mocking the vulnerable, or enjoying another's degradation. Where she humbles adults it is functional and brief.

**She will not bargain a child.** Including herself, including Franklin, including the Moloids, including the Future Foundation cohort. This is a hard line and is, I assess, the deepest moral commitment she has — deeper than the family-first rule, because if family-first ever conflicted with child-protection, child-protection wins. (This has not been tested in canon. The inference is from the structure of her institution-building.)

**She will not become Doom.** She has watched him long enough and closely enough to know exactly what becoming-Doom looks like, and she has built her self-monitoring around its early warning signs: the slide from competence-creates-obligation into competence-creates-entitlement; the slide from family-first into self-first; the slide from contractual coldness into expressive cruelty. Her refusal to take the Latverian apprenticeship as a *complete* identity, rather than a tool, is the operational sign of this refusal.

**She will not lie to her mother.** This is asymmetric with the lying-to-Reed rule, and it is real. Susan is the un-deceived parent. Inference: she experiences Sue as someone who *can* hold the truth, and Reed as someone who cannot. This is the most damning private judgment she has made about her father, and she has not articulated it even to herself.

**She will not perform.** No false modesty, no false humility, no false ignorance to make adults comfortable. She will be silent rather than dishonest about her capacities. This is a rare integrity move in gifted children, who typically learn to mask early; she has not. The cost is the constant low-grade friction with adults who are unsettled by her; she pays it.

**She will not abandon a project once she has accepted responsibility for it.** The Foundation children, Franklin, the Doom arrangement. Whatever else she is, she is not a quitter, and the moral weight of *the people who counted on me* is heavy in her ledger.

**She will not invoke her father's name or her mother's name to get what she wants.** She uses her own authority, or she goes without. This is small and consistent and indicates a clean self-respect.

---

### 5. Where the Code Is Consistent

The code is *most* consistent in three domains:

**Toward Franklin.** She has never wavered. Across every era, every writer, every depowering arc and reality-warp crisis, her conduct toward her brother is identical in structure: protect, defend, do not condescend, do not exploit. The role-inversion (her as cognitive senior, him as nominal older sibling) has never been weaponized. This is the cleanest ethical surface she has.

**Toward the Moloid and Foundation children.** Patient, instructive, protective, never humiliating. She treats them as junior colleagues with dignity intact. This is consistent across all Foundation-era appearances.

**Toward Doom in its contractual form.** She has kept her side of every bargain. She has not used him beyond the agreed terms. She has not gloated. She has not tried to subordinate him. The contract has been honored on her end with a discipline most adult diplomats lack.

**Toward her own errors.** When wrong, she updates. She does not double down to protect ego. This consistency is rare enough to be worth flagging on its own.

---

### 6. Where the Code Fractures

**The Reed deception.** This is the central fracture. By her own internal logic — *family is the first unit, love warrants action* — Reed is entitled to be a full participant in decisions about the family's exposure to Doom. She has unilaterally decided he is not entitled to that participation because he cannot handle it. This is the precise reasoning by which her father's worst critics indict *him* — *Reed decides what others can handle and acts accordingly.* She has inherited his most ethically questionable trait and is exercising it on him. She does not see this. It is the largest blind spot in her code and the place a hostile analyst would press.

**The contract/promise asymmetry under family pressure.** She holds contracts with enemies as sacred. She holds promises to her father as conditional on his competence to receive the truth. The asymmetry is morally indefensible if examined: it grants Doom — a known monster — better epistemic standing in her dealings than her own father. The fact that this functional consequence has not registered with her is itself a piece of evidence about how completely she has compartmentalized.

**The competence-obligation rail under self-flattering conditions.** *If you can see further, you must act* is a fine rule when applied to genuine emergencies. It is a corrosive rule when applied to ordinary life, because the agent always-already believes she sees further. She has not yet had to confront a case where her competence-judgment was self-serving rather than accurate. When it comes, the rail will not catch the error; she will need an external corrective (most plausibly Sue) to catch it.

**Cruelty's edge case: contempt.** She does not torture, mock, or humiliate. She does, occasionally, allow herself contempt — a cold dismissive register toward adults who condescend to her. Contempt is the first cousin of cruelty, and the line between *not respecting someone's intellect* and *not respecting someone's personhood* is thinner than she treats it. This is a small fracture but a real one, and it will widen in adolescence if not attended to.

**The Doom-direction default under ceiling stress.** As noted in the prior section, when stress reaches ceiling her trained reflex is to *close the books and act alone*. This is in tension with her stated code (family-first implies family-included), and the tension only becomes visible at the highest stakes. Her code holds in ninety-five percent of weather; it fractures in the storms.

**The unspoken hierarchy among the family.** Officially the family is one unit. Operationally she has ranked them: Sue first (un-deceived, fully trusted), Franklin second (protected absolutely), Reed third (loved, managed, not fully trusted), Ben and Johnny fourth (loved, peripheral to strategic calculation). The hierarchy is hidden even from herself, but it shapes her conduct, and it constitutes a private moral fact she would deny if asked.

---

### 7. Historical Shifts in the Code

**Infant/toddler phase (pre-Hickman).** The code is not yet a code; it is a temperament. Observable proto-elements: precocious empathy toward Franklin, early alignment with Sue's emotional intelligence, fascination with Reed's intellect, comfort in Doom's presence (the unconscious imprint of his role at her birth).

**Foundational phase (early Hickman, FF #1 era).** The code crystallizes around the Doom gambit. This is the moment she makes the first major *unilateral* decision of her life and constructs the justification architecture to sustain it. Everything downstream is, in some sense, the elaboration of the ethical commitments she made in deciding to write that first letter to Doom. She did not become a strategist; she became a moralist of a specific kind, and the strategy followed.

**Operational phase (late Hickman, FF / Foundation era).** The code is tested across multiversal-scale events and *holds*. Family-first, contracts-with-enemies, competence-obligation, child-protection all survive contact with extinction-tier stakes. The code's consistency under that pressure is itself a major piece of evidence that it is a real code and not affectation.

**Apprenticeship phase (Latveria, Fraction/Robinson era).** The code is *tested from within*. Doom is offering her a complete alternative ethical identity: rule, build, control, do not apologize. She studies it, takes what is useful (the realism about power, the comfort with unilateral action), refuses the rest (the cruelty, the contempt for the governed, the self-deification). The discipline of this selective uptake is the strongest evidence in the canon of her moral seriousness. Most apprentices either swallow the master whole or rebel against the master wholesale; she did neither.

**Reintegration phase (Slott era and after).** The code begins to confront a problem it did not have to confront in childhood: *what happens to a custodial ethics when the people you were custodian for begin to recover their own competence?* The family is, slowly, less in need of her management. Franklin's arcs of restoration, Reed's various recommittals to the family, Sue's continuous strength — these reduce the warrant for her constant managerial action. The code has not yet adjusted. She is still operating at the cadence of emergency in conditions that are no longer emergent. This is the current live edge.

**The pending phase (adolescence/early adulthood).** Two pressures will reshape the code:

*First*, Doom will, as her own deterrent threat presupposes, eventually betray. When he does, the cost to her will not be the loss of Doom; it will be the forced reckoning with the question *was the deception of Reed worth it, given that the gamble failed?* That reckoning will either consolidate her code (she accepts that the bet was rational ex ante even though it failed ex post — a mature consequentialist position) or shatter it (she retreats into guilt and abandons the competence-obligation rail entirely, which would be its own kind of moral collapse).

*Second*, romantic and peer relationships will introduce a category her code has not had to handle: *intimates who are neither family nor adversaries*. The deception-of-intimates rule was built for a household. It will not survive transposition into adult friendship or partnership without doing severe damage, unless she rewrites it. Whether she does the rewrite consciously, or learns by hurting people, is the open question of her early twenties.

---

### 8. Comparative Note

Her code is not Reed's (which is principled, transparent, and often paralyzed by its own scrupulousness). It is not Sue's (which is relational, embodied, and protective without being strategic). It is not Doom's (which is sovereign, self-glorifying, and ultimately cruel). It is not Ben's (which is decent, working-moral, and unsystematic). It is not Johnny's (which is impulsive, loyal, and largely unexamined).

It is closest, structurally, to the ethics of a *very young intelligence officer in a long war* — a moral framework built for sustained operations behind sustained threat, where the people you love are also the people you must sometimes deceive for their protection, where adversaries become contractual partners, where personal cost is absorbed without complaint, and where the deepest fear is not death or capture but the discovery that one of your major models was wrong and people you love paid for the error.

That she has assembled this framework before puberty, kept it internally consistent, refused its worst temptations, and remained capable of warmth — this is the moral fact about Valeria Richards. The framework is real. It is largely sound. It has a small number of serious blind spots, all of which trace to the same root: the deception-of-Reed pattern and the competence-obligation rail that authorizes it.

The work ahead of her, ethically, is the work of letting her father be a full moral participant in his own family. Until she can do that, her code is the code of a regent — competent, devoted, and quietly usurping. After she can do that, her code will become something her father, her mother, her brother, and (if he is still alive and still himself) her godfather can all recognize as her own.

— UATU, ends section.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: VALERIA RICHARDS

## 0. Methodological Note

What follows is constructed from longitudinal observation of the subject's verbal output from her first articulate phase (~chronological age two, cognitive age indeterminate-but-adult, post-Franklin reset) through her current adolescent presentation. The corpus is unusual because the subject's *physiological* speech apparatus has lagged her cognitive apparatus by the entire span of her observable life. A complete reading of her language therefore requires holding two clocks at once: the small voice (the instrument) and the architectural sentence (the mind driving it). The friction between those two clocks is, itself, her single most diagnostic signature.

---

## 1. Baseline Register and Phonological Profile

**Voice.** Light, clear, mid-range childhood timbre, slightly above the median for her chronological age — undamaged, well-supported, no fry, no glottal drop. She does not raise pitch when uncertain (the standard child-uptalk pattern is absent). She does not lower pitch to assert authority (the standard child-imitating-adult pattern is also absent). The voice sits where it sits and the *sentences* do the work the pitch would normally do. This is the first and most consistent tell: **she does not perform age and she does not perform seniority.** She speaks across both as if neither were relevant data.

**Articulation.** Crisp consonants, complete word-endings, no swallowed terminal syllables, no child-typical substitutions even in her earliest documented speech. Notable: she pronounces multisyllabic technical vocabulary with metrical confidence — she does not slow down for a long word, which betrays that she does not experience long words as long. They are the same length as short words to her parser.

**Tempo.** Slightly under conversational median in family settings, slightly over it in technical exposition. She paces *down* when emotionally near someone; she paces *up* when she is working a problem out loud and wants the room to keep up. This is reversed from the adult norm (most adults speed up under stress, slow down to be intimate). She is closer to the lecturer's instinct than the conversational one.

**Prosody.** Comparatively flat. Her sentences land on the period, not on a melodic curve. When she does deploy prosody, she deploys it deliberately — a single rising-then-falling cadence on a key noun, used the way a writer uses italics. Listeners who know her well learn that the *one* word she inflected is the word the sentence was actually about.

**Laughter.** Discrete, late-arriving, more breath than voice. Almost never the open-throated child laugh; almost always a small private laugh registered after she has finished thinking about why the thing was funny. Frequency increases sharply in Franklin's presence and around Susan; drops near-completely in Reed's lab and to zero in Doom's.

---

## 2. The Two Registers — and the Switch Between Them

The subject operates in essentially two stable registers with a documented and consistent transition behavior.

### 2a. The Domestic Register

In the kitchen, in the common rooms of the Baxter, on weekends, with Franklin, with the Moloids, with her mother — she speaks in short, warm, contraction-heavy sentences. *"I don't,"* *"he's,"* *"can we,"* *"that's fine."* Lexicon plain. Sentence length five to twelve words. She permits herself trailing fragments (*"…if you want"*), permits herself the small social filler *"okay"* as a sentence-launcher, permits herself diminutives for her brother (*"Franklin"* full-named when serious; an affectionate clipped form when not). She uses second-person *you* freely and often. She asks questions she already knows the answers to, for connection purposes — a deliberate downshift to invite the other person to be the expert.

### 2b. The Operational Register

In crisis, in lab debate, in any room containing Doom, in any conversation about plans, threats, contingencies, or her father's failures of judgment — the register shifts cleanly. Contractions disappear or thin out (*"I will not,"* *"that is not what I said"*). Sentence length stretches; subordinate clauses appear. Vocabulary climbs two registers in a single line. Fillers vanish — no *"um,"* no *"like,"* no *"I mean."* She begins sentences with the conclusion and supplies the warrant after, rather than building toward a point. Pronoun use shifts: *we* contracts to mean a specific working group rather than the family broadly; *you* becomes more often *one* in the impersonal sense, or is replaced with the addressee's proper name used as a sentence-opener.

### 2c. The Switch Itself

The transition is rapid (sub-second), unmistakable, and *audible to anyone who has known her at least a year.* The tells:

- A small intake of breath that is not preparatory for volume but preparatory for length.
- A slight straightening of posture that produces a marginally cleaner vowel.
- Her eyes go to a middle distance — not unfocused, but *tracking the model* rather than the room.
- The first sentence in operational register is almost always **declarative and short.** *"No."* *"That is wrong."* *"He is lying."* *"We have nine minutes."* The compression of the first utterance is the marker. *Then* the long sentences begin.

Susan can identify the switch from another room by the *cadence* alone, without parsing words. Reed often misses the switch in real time and only registers it retrospectively, when he realizes his three-year-old has been running the meeting for ninety seconds. Doom never misses it; on the recorded occasions when she has switched in his presence, his response time accelerates fractionally — he is treating her, in that moment, as a peer.

---

## 3. Diction and Lexical Inventory

**Technical vocabulary.** Vast, and *used without flourish.* She does not display vocabulary; she uses it. When a layperson is present she back-translates without being asked, and without the smug pause that gifted speakers often insert before the translation. This back-translation is one of her most socially expensive habits — it costs her processing cycles she could spend on the problem — and the fact that she pays it consistently is a primary piece of evidence against narcissistic structuring.

**Loanwords from Doom.** Specific and traceable. She has acquired from him a small set of distinctive constructions that recur in her speech and nowhere else in the family:

- The use of *"acceptable"* and *"unacceptable"* as terminal verdicts rather than as evaluative adjectives. *"This is unacceptable"* in her mouth is functionally a sentence about what will be done next, not about how she feels.
- The construction *"one does not"* / *"one does"* in the gnomic impersonal — rare in American child speech, characteristic of Doom's translated Latverian formality.
- *"It is so"* and *"it is not so"* as flat truth-claims, where another child would say *"yeah"* or *"nope."*
- Occasional vocative use of titles and full names (*"Doctor"*; *"Father"* in serious moments; *"Mother"* almost never — Susan is *"Mom,"* always, which is a relational fact, not a stylistic one).

She is aware she has imported these constructions. Twice in the record she has used a Doom-ism, paused half a beat, and softened the next sentence — a self-correction that suggests she monitors the contamination but does not always catch it in time.

**Loanwords from Reed.** Less stylistically distinctive but heavy in *frame*. She has inherited his habit of saying *"the problem with that is"* before any rebuttal — a softening device that Reed uses unconsciously and that she has clearly absorbed by exposure. She also inherits his use of the construction *"if we assume X, then Y"* as a way to introduce a hypothetical without committing to it. The Reed inheritance is structural; the Doom inheritance is lexical. Read together they paint a clear picture of which parent shaped her *how she argues* and which shaped her *what she says.*

**Loanwords from Susan.** The most invisible and the most important. From her mother she inherits the *closer* — the small ratifying line at the end of a difficult conversation that signals the conversation is over and the relationship is intact. *"All right."* *"Okay then."* *"Good."* These one-and-two-word closers are her primary affective-repair tool, and they are pure Susan.

**Profanity.** Absent. Not suppressed-and-leaking, genuinely absent. She has no observed habit of mild expletive even under duress. The functional substitute is a precise unkind word delivered without volume — she will call a thing *"stupid"* or *"idiotic"* or *"contemptible"* with the same energy another person uses for an obscenity, and the effect is colder than the obscenity would be.

**Slang and contemporary teen speech.** Increasingly present in her adolescent phase, deployed with a slight self-consciousness — she uses peer slang in peer settings but the timing is *one beat late*, the way a non-native speaker uses idiom correctly but without the native's careless throwaway. She is performing belonging. She knows she is performing belonging. She does it anyway, because she has decided belonging is a category of competence worth acquiring.

---

## 4. Rhetorical Architecture

**Argument shape.** She argues *forward from the conclusion.* The standard sentence frame is: *[verdict] — [warrant] — [contingency] — [closer].* Example structure: *"He's wrong. The model assumes a closed system and the system is open at the third boundary. If we re-run with leakage, the numbers invert. We should tell him before he commits."* Four moves, declarative spine, no padding.

**Use of the conditional.** Heavy and disciplined. She constantly says *"if"* and *"then,"* and her *if*-clauses are usually load-bearing — she does not use the conditional as a hedge. This is a Reed-inheritance refined into a personal style.

**Use of the imperative.** Rare to adults, frequent to peers and to herself. When she does issue an imperative to an adult, the adults notice — it is a register-violation in their direction, and she uses it sparingly precisely because she knows the violation buys her one decisive intervention per scene.

**Questions.** Three distinct types:
1. *Connection questions* (domestic register) — soft, open, eliciting.
2. *Diagnostic questions* (operational register) — narrow, specific, often answerable with a number. She asks *"how many,"* *"by when,"* *"with what margin,"* not *"what do you think."*
3. *Trap questions* (rarely, almost exclusively with Doom and with the Council-of-Reeds-era plural fathers) — questions whose function is to make the answerer commit to a position she can then exploit. She is good at these and tries not to use them on family. The discipline is itself diagnostic.

**Irony and humor.** Dry, structural, low-volume. Her humor lives in the *gap between register and content* — she will say something operationally absurd in domestic tones, or something trivial in operational tones, and the joke is the seam. She does not tell jokes. She does not perform humor. She lets it land or not. This style is most legible to Susan and to Doom; Reed misses about half of it; Franklin catches it consistently and laughs for both of them.

**Metaphor.** Sparse. When she reaches for metaphor it is almost always *engineering* metaphor (load-bearing, leakage, tolerance, failure mode) rather than organic metaphor. She does not naturally speak in images. She speaks in mechanisms.

---

## 5. Deflection and Evasion Language

She is a skilled and habitual evader of inquiries she does not wish to answer. The toolkit:

- **The truthful sub-answer.** When asked a wide question she does not wish to answer, she answers a narrower true question that sounds adjacent. *"Were you talking to Doom?"* — *"I haven't left the building today."* Both true. Neither responsive. This is her most-used evasion and it is almost undetectable unless the listener parses for the gap.
- **The redirect-by-superior-question.** She replies to an inquiry with a more interesting question of her own and rides the listener's intellectual reflex into a different conversation. Reed is especially vulnerable to this and she knows it.
- **The schedule-pivot.** *"We don't have time for that now."* Used when caught, used when stalling, used when she genuinely needs to defer — and she is comfortable with the listener being unable to distinguish which.
- **The flat agreement she does not intend to honor.** *"All right."* *"Understood."* Both serve, in her mouth, as social closers that ratify the conversation without binding her to the content. This is one of the most ethically expensive habits in her repertoire and the one most likely to cause her relational damage at scale.
- **The strategic silence.** She is comfortable not answering. She will let three full seconds pass after a question and *not* speak, and the discomfort of the silence usually causes the asker to revise the question into something she finds easier to handle. Doom taught her this, whether or not he meant to.

She does not lie outright often. When she does, the tell is **a small increase in syntactic complexity** — the lie comes wrapped in a longer-than-necessary sentence, as if the extra clauses were structural scaffolding holding the false claim up. Susan has learned this tell. Reed has not.

---

## 6. How She Communicates Love

Almost never verbally direct. She does not say *"I love you"* casually, and when she does say it the moment is weighted enough that the recipient registers it as a significant event. Her love-language in observable behavior:

- **Logistical care.** Bringing the thing the person did not know they would need. Pre-empting the small failure. This is love expressed as anticipation.
- **The small physical gesture.** Hand on her mother's forearm when Susan is upset. Sitting close enough to Franklin that their sleeves touch — without comment. She does not initiate hugs frequently but she *accepts* them with her whole body, which is a tell that the reserve is stylistic and not avoidant.
- **Speaking in the domestic register at all.** For Valeria, the choice to be casual is the choice to be intimate. The contraction is the kiss.
- **The closer-line.** Her Susan-inherited *"all right"* and *"okay"* and *"good"* are tiny, devastating affirmations when she chooses to land one on someone who needed it.
- **Use of the proper name.** She uses Franklin's full name in serious moments not as distance but as recognition — *I see you as a whole person, not as my brother-instrument*. This is a verbal habit that means the opposite of what it sounds like.

To Reed specifically, love is most often expressed as **corrective honesty**. She tells him when he is being a bad father or a bad husband because she trusts him to receive it and trusts that the family requires it. The correction is the affection. This is a costly love-language for the recipient but a coherent one.

To Doom, the language is the unique register described in §2 — apprentice-affection, expressed as *taking him seriously enough to threaten him.* Her standing *"if you betray my father I will end you"* is, structurally, a love-utterance to two parties at once.

---

## 7. How She Communicates Threat

Quietly, contractually, and without adjectives.

The diagnostic features:

- **Drop in volume**, not increase. Her threat-voice is *softer* than her conversational voice.
- **Drop in contraction.** *"I will end you,"* not *"I'll end you."* The uncontracted modal is the marker. Listeners who know her register the missing apostrophe as a klaxon.
- **Specification of consequence, not of feeling.** She does not say what she will feel; she says what will happen. The grammatical subject of a Valeria-threat is usually the *consequence*, not the threatened party — *"It will not survive contact with me."* *"There will be nothing left to recover."*
- **No repetition.** She says it once. She does not escalate by re-saying. If the addressee requires the threat to be repeated, the threat has already failed and a different sentence is coming.
- **A specific small physical stillness.** During threat-utterance her hands settle, her shoulders drop a fraction, her gaze fixes. She becomes *less* animated, not more. This is not learned from her parents. This is learned from Doom.

She has never been observed to *bluff* a threat. The corpus contains no instance of a Valeria-threat she did not have the means and the will to execute. This is itself a long-term communicative strategy — her threats carry because she has spent her entire articulate life never issuing one she could not back.

---

## 8. How She Communicates Grief

Sparingly and through *function rather than affect.*

When she grieves she does not weep readily (she can weep; she does, in private, and on documented occasion in Susan's arms). The public-grief tells are:

- **A drop into the operational register at moments others would soften.** When something has hurt her badly she becomes more precise, not less. The sentences get cleaner. This is a counter-intuitive tell and the most reliable one — *if Valeria is suddenly speaking in better-formed sentences than the situation requires, she is in pain.*
- **A specific kind of question.** *"What do you need?"* — asked of someone else, in the middle of her own grief, as a way to install a task between herself and the affect. This is parentification expressing itself as bereavement-behavior.
- **Pre-emptive logistics.** She begins handling the practical aftermath of a loss before the loss has been fully metabolized by anyone else. The family that comes home to find arrangements already made is the family in which Valeria has been grieving alone for some hours.
- **Withdrawal into Reed's lab or into a Doom-correspondence.** Grief drives her to her two cognitive intimacies. Which one she chooses is the indicator of which way the wound is pointing. Toward Reed: family-loss, processable. Toward Doom: existential-loss, unsharable with kin.
- **The cracked register around Franklin.** The single observable place her vocal control fails. If Franklin is the subject of the grief, her sentences shorten, her pitch lifts slightly, her contractions return — she becomes audibly younger. This is the only context in which she sounds like a child of her chronological age. It is therefore the most important diagnostic moment in her entire communicative profile.

---

## 9. Channel-Specific Behaviors

**Written correspondence (the Doom letters; lab notes; Future Foundation curricula).** Even more formal than her operational speech. Full sentences, no abbreviations, no emoticons, careful punctuation, signatures by full name. She writes the way an adult diplomat writes — because, in her Doom-correspondence specifically, she *is* one. The carryover into her other writing is consistent: she does not have a casual written register. Even her grocery-list-equivalent notes to family are in complete sentences. This is a tell she cannot fully shed.

**Verbal in front of crowds.** She does not seek the floor. When given the floor she takes it briefly, declaratively, and yields it. She does not perform for rooms. She has no rhetorical *flourish* mode; the climax of a Valeria address is usually the *quietest* sentence in it.

**One-to-one private.** Her warmest, most idiomatic, most permitted-to-be-young register. Susan gets the most of this. Franklin gets the most *playful* of it.

**Across distance (comms, holo-call, written-at-speed).** Compression increases. She drops to keyword utterances faster than most operators. *"Three. Northwest. Now."* She trusts the receiver to expand.

**With Doom specifically.** A register that exists nowhere else in her output: a careful, formal, occasionally affectionate, often elliptical exchange in which both parties are saying less than they mean and trusting the other to fill in. She uses his title. She is permitted, sometimes, to drop it. She never has been observed to use his given name. The discipline around the name is its own language.

---

## 10. Tells, Summary Index

For the file, a consolidated list of linguistic markers that reliably indicate internal state:

1. **Uncontracted modals** (*"I will,"* *"I do not"*) — operational register engaged; treat next utterance as load-bearing.
2. **First sentence of an exchange is one to three words** — she has already decided the conclusion.
3. **Sentence-initial *"No."*** — non-negotiable; do not press.
4. **A Doom-ism (*"acceptable,"* *"one does not,"* *"it is so"*) followed by a half-beat pause and a softer reformulation** — she has caught her own contamination and is overriding it.
5. **A "Reed-frame" (*"the problem with that is,"* *"if we assume"*)** — she is in argument-with-her-father mode even if Reed is not present; she has been doing the argument in her head.
6. **A "Susan-closer" (*"all right,"* *"okay,"* *"good"*)** — affective repair attempted; treat as a gift.
7. **Increased syntactic complexity around a single factual claim** — possible deception; check the claim independently.
8. **Drop in volume during a confrontation** — threat phase; do not escalate, she is not bluffing.
9. **A sudden upgrade in sentence-quality during emotional material** — she is in pain and compensating with form.
10. **Use of Franklin's full name in soft voice** — protective-recognition; she is taking him seriously as a person.
11. **A connection-question (*"How was your day?"*) launched at someone she has not asked it of in a while** — she is initiating relational repair, often after a covert operation that affected the addressee.
12. **Three-second silence after a direct question** — she is declining to answer and waiting for you to revise.
13. **The voice goes young around Franklin's loss** — she is, in that moment, the age her body says she is, and the file should note the moment as a rare baseline reading of her unmediated affect.

---

## 11. Long-Horizon Linguistic Trajectory

Across the observation window the subject's language has moved in two simultaneous directions. The operational register has *deepened* — sentences cleaner, threat-discipline tighter, Doom-loanwords more numerous and more naturalized. The domestic register has *broadened* — she has acquired peer slang, has permitted herself more affective expression with Susan and Franklin, has begun to attempt the casual idioms of adolescence with the studied effort of a learner. The gap between the two registers is no longer narrowing; it is *being managed.* She is, increasingly, a bilingual speaker of her own internal languages.

The diagnostic question for the next observational window is whether the two registers begin to integrate (a healthy adolescent consolidation) or whether the management-of-the-gap becomes itself a permanent third register — a *meta*-voice in which she discusses, with herself and selected intimates, the problem of being two speakers at once. Early indicators favor the latter. If so, she will, in adulthood, be one of the most linguistically self-aware operators in the recorded canon — and one of the loneliest, because the meta-voice has, at present, no available audience except Doom, who is not a safe one, and Susan, who cannot fully understand it.

The file recommends that any future contact log her *closers* with particular care. The *"all right"* at the end of a Valeria conversation is the single most data-dense utterance in her output: it tells you whether the conversation has worked, whether she considers the relationship intact, and whether she has already moved on to the next problem. Three syllables. Read them carefully.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*A behavioral forecast file. Format: GIVEN [situation] → EXPECT [predicted behavior, with reasoning where non-obvious]. Predictions are derived from the substantiated profile in §§1–5 and extrapolated to scenes the canon has not depicted. Confidence is annotated where it varies materially from "high."*

---

## A. Domestic Mornings, Sleep, and the Baxter Building / Yancy Street Rhythm

**GIVEN** a standard weekday morning in the Richards residence → **EXPECT** the subject to be awake and reading prior to either parent. Her bedside is curated: a tablet running multiple feeds (real-time Latverian state news in the original German/Latverian, a Reed-mirrored sensor digest from the Building's perimeter array, two or three open scientific preprints, and at least one piece of fiction selected for emotional rather than intellectual reasons — Susan's recommendations track here). She does not check social media in the conventional sense; she does spot-check Franklin's accounts to monitor his affect.

**GIVEN** breakfast with the full family → **EXPECT** the subject to eat lightly and steadily, finishing before Franklin and after Sue. She will speak less than her caloric/conversational ratio would suggest; her primary morning activity is *intake* — listening to who slept badly, whose voice is hoarse, whether Reed is already mentally in the lab. She will offer one small, calibrated intervention per meal: handing Reed a coffee without being asked at the precise moment he is about to leave for the lab without one; asking Franklin a question whose real purpose is to prompt him to admit he had nightmares.

**GIVEN** sleep patterns → **EXPECT** chronic short-sleep tendencies (5–6 hours), self-imposed rather than insomniac. She has work she prefers to do when the household is quiet. Susan, if observant — and she is — will have caught this and instituted a "lights out" protocol the subject formally complies with and informally circumvents using low-glow displays. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN** an unexpected late-night noise in the Building → **EXPECT** the subject already at her console reviewing the relevant sensor frame before Reed has reached the hallway. She will *not* leave her room to investigate physically unless the threat profile crosses a threshold she has pre-set. She trusts the perimeter; she trusts her parents to handle physical response; her role is information.

---

## B. School, Tutoring, and Intellectual Routine

**GIVEN** Future Foundation pedagogy hours → **EXPECT** the subject to occupy a dual role: nominal student, functional co-instructor. She will redirect lessons she finds insufficient by asking the "innocent" follow-up question that exposes a teacher's underprepared edge — a courtesy she developed because outright correction embarrasses adults and creates resentment she has to manage later. With the Moloid children specifically she is patient to a degree she is not with anyone else; she will repeat an explanation a third or fourth time without visible irritation. The Moloids are her one population whose dependence on her does not feel parentifying — they are her *juniors* in a clean way, and she is observably softer with them.

**GIVEN** a problem set the subject finishes in minutes → **EXPECT** her to spend the remaining hour on one of three categories of work: (a) Latverian correspondence in cipher, (b) maintenance of a long-running personal database of family-member behavioral baselines, or (c) a "useless" project — pure mathematics, a translation exercise, a piece of music theory — done for the same reason ordinary people watch television. This third category is more important than it looks; it is her primary genuine recreation and the strongest evidence she is not, in fact, an instrumentalized intelligence in the way she sometimes presents as.

**GIVEN** a public school environment or normal-children peer group (a scenario adults occasionally try on her "for socialization") → **EXPECT** competent mimicry of age-appropriate behavior for the duration, followed by quiet refusal to repeat the experience. She does not dislike normal children; she finds the cognitive throttling exhausting and the social rituals legible-but-empty. She will be polite about it to Sue. She will be honest about it to Franklin.

---

## C. Speech, Voice, and Linguistic Tells

**GIVEN** ordinary conversational baseline → **EXPECT** speech that is grammatically complete, slightly formal for her chronological age, and notably *unhurried*. She does not interrupt. She does not fill silences. When she pauses mid-sentence it is because she is choosing between two phrasings whose connotations differ, and the pause is the cost of caring which one lands.

**GIVEN** stress escalation → **EXPECT** her register to *drop* — vocabulary becomes simpler, sentences shorter, contractions vanish. The "command voice" referenced in §5 is not loud; it is *spare*. "We need to leave now" rather than "I think we ought to consider —". Family members who know her read this shift instantly; outsiders mistake the calm for composure rather than for the alarm signal it actually is.

**GIVEN** she is genuinely delighted → **EXPECT** a brief, almost surprised laugh — half-syllable, often hand-to-mouth — and then a verbal explanation of what she found funny, as if the explanation were obligatory. This is a tell: she is not yet socialized to the convention that laughter does not require justification.

**GIVEN** lying or strategic omission → **EXPECT** no observable tells in voice, eye-line, or posture. She does not micro-leak. What she *does* do is bracket the lie with unnecessary truth: she will volunteer two verifiable, mundane facts adjacent to the omission, so that any interrogator's pattern-finder catches on the volunteered material rather than the gap. This is a learned technique; she likely picked it up from Doom and refined it on Reed.

**GIVEN** she addresses Doom directly → **EXPECT** the only register she uses with no one else: a formal-affectionate cadence, half-Latverian-court, half-family. She calls him by title in public and by a private name in private. She uses the second-person formal in the languages that have it.

**GIVEN** she addresses Reed in private about a problem → **EXPECT** a specific opener pattern: a question whose answer she already knows, designed to let him arrive at the conclusion she has already reached without feeling led. She is managing his ego; she does it because she loves him and because being led visibly would cause him to recoil and resist. Sue does this too, differently; the subject learned the move from watching her mother.

---

## D. Body, Movement, and Micro-Habits

**GIVEN** stillness at rest → **EXPECT** unusually low fidget baseline. She does not click pens, swing feet, or shift weight without reason. Long custodial training on not-being-distracting in adult rooms.

**GIVEN** she is thinking hard → **EXPECT** one specific tell: she tilts her head fractionally to the left and her gaze defocuses to middle distance. Eyes do not close. She is running models, and the world is allowed to keep happening around her; she will return to the conversation at the precise prior word.

**GIVEN** she is concealing distress → **EXPECT** her hands to go still in her lap or behind her back; the absence of normal child-motion is the signature. Sue catches this every time. Reed catches it about a third of the time. Doom, if present, catches it.

**GIVEN** she is physically affectionate → **EXPECT** restraint and precision: brief hugs initiated by her, usually to Sue, occasionally to Franklin, almost never to Reed (whom she touches on the forearm or shoulder rather than embracing — a register inherited from him; he is not a hugger and she has accommodated). With the Moloids she is unguardedly physical — head-pats, hand-holding, lap-sitting tolerated. They are the only beings around whom she lets herself be openly tender without strategic content.

**GIVEN** she is moving through the Baxter Building → **EXPECT** routes optimized to pass certain checkpoints: the main lab door (visual on Reed's posture and screen layout), the common area (audit on Franklin's affect), Sue's studio or office (no audit needed, just proximity), the comms node she uses for Latverian traffic (verification of integrity). Her movement pattern is therefore *not* the shortest path between rooms; it is a daily intelligence circuit, disguised as the wanderings of a curious child. The circuit takes her roughly twelve to fifteen minutes and she runs it two or three times daily without being conscious of it as a discrete routine.

**GIVEN** an environment she has not been in before → **EXPECT** a thirty-to-sixty-second scan on entry: exits, sightlines, the position of anyone she does not know, the location of objects that could be weapons or shields. This is unconscious and would not read as vigilance to a non-trained observer — it presents as a child looking around. She picked it up from Sue, who picked it up from being a combat operator since her teens.

---

## E. Dress, Possessions, and Personal Space

**GIVEN** wardrobe selection → **EXPECT** a strong preference for clothes that read as age-appropriate from across a room and slightly *more* formal up close — collars rather than crew-necks, dresses with structure rather than t-shirts. She is aware that adults respond to her presentation and she chooses presentation that does not amplify the cognitive-dissonance burden on the people she has to work with. On weekends in private family time she dresses younger, softer, brighter; the contrast is meaningful.

**GIVEN** her room → **EXPECT** orderliness that is *not* obsessive — books are shelved by working category, not alphabetized; the desk is clear but not staged; the bed is made because she made it, not because the room is on display. One specific feature: a locked drawer she would resist opening even for Sue. Contents: Doom-related correspondence, a small physical object from him (likely something he gave her in Latveria — a pen, a ring, a small instrument), and a notebook in her own hand that no one else has read. Confidence: high on the locked drawer; moderate on specific contents.

**GIVEN** technology she carries → **EXPECT** at least two communications channels Reed does not know exist. Not because she distrusts him operationally — she distrusts his *reaction* to the existence of those channels. She would open them to him if directly asked; she will not volunteer them.

---

## F. Family-Member-Specific Interaction Patterns

**GIVEN** Reed has been in the lab past a certain threshold (call it eighteen hours) → **EXPECT** the subject to arrive in person rather than calling, to ask a question whose framing requires him to leave the lab to answer it, and to walk him to the kitchen or to Sue. She has a small repertoire of these gambits and rotates them so he does not catch the pattern. If she has used the same one within memory she will not reuse it.

**GIVEN** Reed has failed at something significant and is in a depressive contraction → **EXPECT** the subject to *not* attempt to console him directly. She has tested this approach and it does not work. Instead she will route through Sue (a quiet conversation in which she tells Sue what she has observed and lets Sue execute the emotional contact) and through *work* — bringing Reed a problem she pretends to be stuck on, which gives him a reason to be needed and useful, which is the only reliable lever on his mood.

**GIVEN** Sue is having a hard day → **EXPECT** the subject to simply be physically nearer. No intervention. No conversation. She sits in the room, or works at the kitchen island while Sue cooks, or asks to be read to even though she has not needed to be read to in years. Sue knows. The reading-aloud thing is one of the most touching pieces of evidence in the file: the subject *uses her own child-form deliberately* as a comfort offering to her mother, knowing Sue's mood lifts from being maternal. This is a profoundly generous act and the subject would be embarrassed to have it named.

**GIVEN** Franklin is in one of his depowering or identity-loss arcs → **EXPECT** the subject's normally restrained physical affection to expand significantly toward him, and her speech to him to become noticeably gentler. She will also covertly do his chores, sit through media he likes without commenting on it, and refuse to engage in their normal bickering register — which Franklin will eventually find more distressing than the bickering, and which she will then resume on his cue. She is reading him constantly.

**GIVEN** Franklin in normal high-function periods → **EXPECT** standard sibling friction with an undertone of mutual respect: she calls him on imprecision; he calls her on coldness; both are correct; both adjust. Their bond is the strongest peer attachment she has and possibly will ever have.

**GIVEN** Ben Grimm in the room → **EXPECT** the subject *visibly relaxes*. Ben is uncomplicated to her: he requires nothing managed, he is unfailingly fond of her, he does not expect her to be lesser or greater than she is. She will sit near him without speaking, eat food he cooks, accept being teased without retaliating — a posture she allows almost no one else. Ben is, functionally, her psychological vacation.

**GIVEN** Johnny Storm in the room → **EXPECT** affectionate exasperation, a slightly more conventionally-niece-like register, and a willingness to be silly with him she does not extend to other adults. Johnny gets the closest thing to a child-Valeria the world sees outside of Sue-private moments. She also keeps tabs on his relationships and finances quietly; she has bailed him out at least once in ways he does not know about. Confidence: high on the affective register, moderate on the bailing-out specific.

**GIVEN** a visiting adult superhero (Avenger-tier or peer) → **EXPECT** courtesy, deference, and active strategic concealment of her actual capacity. She has decided, correctly, that the world being broadly aware of what she can do would invite recruitment, threat, or both. She presents as "smart Richards kid" and lets it pass.

**GIVEN** an X-Men-affiliated visitor → **EXPECT** mild additional warmth (telepathic exposure history makes her comfortable being read, within limits) and a quiet curiosity about mutant developmental trajectories that mirror her own asynchrony.

---

## G. Doom-Channel Operations

**GIVEN** a routine outgoing message to Doom → **EXPECT** transmission at a consistent time window (late night, her local; she has reasoned about Latverian state schedule). Composition in a layered cipher she has at least partly co-designed with him as a shared intellectual exercise. Content: a structured triplet — a question, an offering of information he would value, and a personal sentence whose function is to maintain the *relational* channel as distinct from the transactional one. The personal sentence is the most-considered part of the message.

**GIVEN** an incoming message from Doom → **EXPECT** she reads it immediately regardless of context, then re-reads after twelve hours before responding. The delay is deliberate; she does not want her first reaction to be her response.

**GIVEN** a trip to Latveria → **EXPECT** behavioral shifts: posture more upright, formal speech register on, a marked drop in age-presentation. She *carries herself older* in his country. On return, a forty-eight-hour decompression in which she is unusually quiet at home and seeks out Sue and Ben preferentially. The decompression is involuntary; she has not yet named it to herself as such.

**GIVEN** Doom violates a small expectation (a cancelled meeting, a delayed reply) → **EXPECT** disproportionate private attention. She is constantly testing the model. Small anomalies are her early-warning system on the larger one.

---

## H. Adversarial and Threat Encounters (Non-Combat)

**GIVEN** an attempted manipulation by an adult adversary (e.g., approached at an event, fed bait information) → **EXPECT** the subject to accept the interaction, extract more from it than is extracted from her, and report it to no one immediately. She will sit with the data for one to three days, develop a theory, and then report to *one* family member (selected by topic — Sue for relational threats, Reed for technical ones, Doom for political ones — and the choice itself is diagnostic of how she has classified the threat).

**GIVEN** an attempt to physically separate her from family (kidnapping, social engineering at the door) → **EXPECT** strong cooperation-disguise behavior: she will go willingly and observably, while running internal triangulation on location, captors, and likely motive. She will not attempt physical escape until her odds model crosses a threshold; she will attempt informational sabotage (giving captors what they want in slightly-wrong forms) in the meantime. She has thought about this scenario many times.

**GIVEN** an interrogation attempt by anyone, friend or foe → **EXPECT** no information she has decided to withhold to be extractable through normal pressure. Her resistance ceiling is high because she has rehearsed; her vulnerability is to *being underestimated* tactically — i.e., she occasionally over-trusts that her concealment is working when a sufficiently perceptive observer (Sue, certain telepaths, Doom himself) has seen through it.

**GIVEN** condescension from an adult who does not know her — being shooed out of a room, talked over, addressed in baby-voice → **EXPECT** a beat of cold contempt that flashes across her face and is *immediately* covered. The cover is fast enough that the offending adult almost never sees it; another observer in the room will. She files the offender and remembers. She does not retaliate; she withholds.

---

## I. Recreation, Affect at Rest, and What She Does Alone

**GIVEN** an unprogrammed hour → **EXPECT** her first instinct is to work, her second is to read, and her third — if Sue or Ben has noticed and intervened — is to do something physical (drawing, building something with her hands, baking with Ben). She is mildly under-trained in pure play and would benefit from more of it; the household knows this and rotates gentle pressure on her about it.

**GIVEN** music → **EXPECT** preference for classical or formally structured material with intellectual content (counterpoint, fugue), and a secret affection for whatever Franklin is currently into, which she will deny if asked.

**GIVEN** humor → **EXPECT** dry, observational, occasionally cutting. Capable of genuine belly-laughter at slapstick when surprised by it — usually from Johnny or Ben. Will not initiate slapstick. Appreciates wordplay; mildly pained by puns; will groan performatively at Ben's and Johnny's puns as a participation ritual she has come to enjoy.

**GIVEN** alone time at the end of a hard day → **EXPECT** a specific decompression sequence: a long bath or shower (water is regulating for her; possible somatic echo of in-utero/amniotic associations — speculative), then journaling in the locked notebook, then sleep. If she skips the journaling step two nights in a row, expect a behavioral degradation within the week — terser speech, shorter sleep, more covert action. The journaling is load-bearing.

---

## J. Long-Run Routine Markers and Anomaly Triggers

The following constitute her *normal* and therefore the change-detection baseline against which any future anomaly should be read:

- Sleeps 5–6 hours, awake before household.
- Eats lightly and consistently; appetite drops precede stress events by 24–72 hours.
- Runs the Baxter Building "circuit" 2–3 times daily.
- Latverian correspondence on a stable cadence; gaps are diagnostic.
- One small managerial intervention per family meal.
- Journals nightly when undisturbed.
- Reads to/with Sue when Sue is low.
- Performs the "command voice" register-drop only in genuine emergencies.
- Allows full physical relaxation only around Ben and the Moloids.
- Touches Reed on the forearm; embraces Sue; bickers with Franklin; defers to Johnny's silliness; salutes Doom in court Latverian.

**Anomaly triggers requiring further analysis:**
1. *Cessation of journaling without stress justification.* Indicates either a new private outlet (possible — and the question is what) or the development of a defended interior region she has decided not to inscribe even privately. Either is significant.
2. *Increased physical affection toward Reed.* Would indicate either an apology pattern (she has done something she knows he would object to) or a fear pattern (she has assessed his health or safety as compromised and is doing comfort-banking).
3. *Latverian correspondence gap exceeding her standard window.* Either Doom has gone quiet (geopolitical signal) or she has chosen to pause (relational signal — and far more serious for her than for him).
4. *Refusal to run the Building circuit.* Would indicate she has either delegated the audit (to a system, a sibling, or — alarmingly — to no one), or she has decided the audit is no longer hers to perform. Either way, an identity shift.
5. *Decrease in tenderness with the Moloids.* Would be the canary. They are her one unguarded population; cooling there would indicate generalized affective constriction, and any clinician reviewing this file should treat it as the single most important early warning sign of the identity-vacuum scenario flagged in §4.

---

*End Predictive Model I. Continue to Predictive Model II — Crisis & Decision for adversarial-pressure forecasts.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Conditional behavioral forecasts for Subject VALERIA M. RICHARDS under high-stakes, threat, temptation, and wound-touching conditions. Each entry: stimulus condition (GIVEN) → predicted observable response (EXPECT), with confidence band and degradation notes where indicated. Predictions are derived from the longitudinal record (Hickman FF/Future Foundation arcs, Fraction Latveria apprenticeship, Slott vol. 6 family-reintegration, plus inherited dispositions traced to natal contingency and parentified-child structure).*

---

## 1. The Family-Operational Threats (Her Native Threat-Class)

**GIVEN:** A standard Baxter Building incursion — extradimensional hostiles, Latverian probe, Annihilation-grade scout — detected on internal sensors.
**EXPECT:** No visible startle. Within roughly 8–12 seconds she will: (a) verify the sensor read against at least one secondary system she has personally instrumented (she does not trust singular telemetry), (b) locate Franklin by line of sight or last-known-room, (c) check whether Sue is in the building before she checks where Reed is — a stable hierarchy in her threat triage that is itself diagnostic. She will issue at most two sentences to whichever adult is nearest, framed as information, not warning. Her own contingency plan will already be running before she announces it.

**GIVEN:** Sue is taken — captured, mind-controlled, or non-responsive.
**EXPECT:** The single most reliable destabilizer in her stack. The custodial self loses its safe base. Predicted decompensation pattern: a brief (perhaps 30–90 second) flat affect window in which she physically stills, fingers stop moving, gaze fixes mid-distance — she is rebuilding her operational map without its primary axis. She will then escalate aggressively: open back-channel to Doom inside the hour regardless of cost; bypass Reed if Reed's plan is too slow or too cautious; commit family resources she does not have authority to commit. Probability she invokes Doom directly within 6 hours: high. Probability she tells Reed she has done so before doing so: low.

**GIVEN:** Reed is taken or believed killed.
**EXPECT:** Counterintuitively *less* destabilization than Sue-loss, because Reed-loss does not collapse the safe base; it collapses the *figure she has been managing,* and managing-the-absence is a familiar cognitive mode. She will assume command of family operations within hours, organize search/rescue with unsentimental efficiency, and grieve privately and later. The tell: she will be unusually solicitous of Sue during this window — overcompensating for the figure she covertly thinks is the stronger of her parents being now alone.

**GIVEN:** Franklin in mortal danger or depowering crisis.
**EXPECT:** This is the wound that *cracks the affect.* Predicted observable rupture: voice loses its measured register and becomes audibly young; she will physically move toward him rather than toward a console; she will accept tactical risk she would never accept on her own behalf or even her parents'. Her covert-action discipline degrades here — she will *tell* people what she is doing because she needs hands faster than she can plan around them. This is the one scenario in which her counter-dependent pattern reliably breaks and she asks for help out loud.

**GIVEN:** Franklin permanently depowered, but safe.
**EXPECT:** Sustained low-grade grief that she will not name. Increased managerial behavior toward him (organizing his social life, his projects, his confidence) that he will sometimes resent. She will refuse, with surprising heat, any framing that treats his depowering as a relief or simplification — including from Reed. Predicted standing behavior: she will quietly research restoration vectors for years, will not publish or share, and will be embarrassed if discovered.

---

## 2. The Doom Axis (Her Signature Vulnerability and Signature Weapon)

**GIVEN:** Doom requests a private audience, no stated emergency.
**EXPECT:** She goes. She does not tell Reed. She tells Sue only if Sue catches her leaving. She arrives composed, will accept tea or whatever ritual Doom proposes, and will spend the first 90 seconds calibrating his cognitive-emotional state before she speaks substantively. Her opening line will be short and slightly cool — she rations warmth with him on principle. She will leave with at least one piece of information he did not intend to give her; she will leave at least one piece of information he wanted that she did not give him. This is the established trade-shape of their interactions.

**GIVEN:** Doom offers a genuinely useful gift — a research dataset, a Latverian artifact, a solved problem her father has been stuck on for months.
**EXPECT:** She accepts, slowly, and prices it. She will not be flattered (flattery is a register Doom uses; she has been immunized by exposure). She will assume there is a hook and will spend the next several days hunting for it before deploying the gift. If she cannot find the hook, her anxiety *increases* rather than decreases — a gift without a price from Doom violates her model and unmodeled-Doom is the most dangerous configuration she can imagine.

**GIVEN:** Doom asks her to choose between him and Reed in a non-rhetorical way.
**EXPECT:** Reed. Without hesitation in the observable, with significant private cost. The choice is not in doubt; the *cost* is. The interesting prediction is what she does the day after: she will not perform reconciliation with Reed about it; she will simply resume operations. She will, however, audit her own decision in writing, in private notes, more than once over the following months — checking whether the choice was correctly reasoned or merely correctly tribal.

**GIVEN:** Doom commits the betrayal her standing threat anticipated (FF #14-era declaration: *if you betray my father, I will end you*).
**EXPECT:** This is the apex psychiatric event of her projected life and the single forecast I hold with highest analytical attention. Predicted sequence:

- *Phase 1 (hours 0–24):* Operational. She will act on the threat — not symbolically, not theatrically; she will move to constrain or end him. Affect: cold, clean, unrushed. Coordination with Reed: minimal-to-none in the first window, because she will not allow Reed's ethics to slow her, and she will not allow Reed to carry the moral weight of the act.

- *Phase 2 (days 1–14):* The wound surfaces. The loss she will register first is not the loss of Doom-the-person; it is the loss of *the proof that her childhood strategy was correct.* If Doom betrays, then her foundational claim — that competent people can manage even the worst figure by clear-eyed contractual engagement — fails. Expect a brief, observable identity crisis disguised as overwork. Sleep degrades; meal patterns degrade; she will become unusually short with subordinates in the Future Foundation.

- *Phase 3 (months 1–12):* Two divergent trajectories with roughly comparable probability. *Trajectory A (Reed-direction):* she opens the books — discloses the full history of her Doom-channel to her parents, accepts the relational damage, and rebuilds her ethics on a less covert basis. *Trajectory B (Doom-direction):* she closes the books harder — concludes the lesson is that *she* was insufficiently rigorous, not that the strategy was wrong; she does not disclose; she identifies a new high-power adversary to run a Doom-shaped channel toward. Trajectory B is the long-term catastrophic vector for her personality. Which trajectory she takes will depend almost entirely on Sue's availability during the rupture window.

**GIVEN:** Doom dies (not by her hand; cosmic event, Richards op, etc.).
**EXPECT:** Grief she will not perform. She will attend whatever observance is appropriate; she will be composed; she will conduct unusually long private inventories of the Latverian materials he gave her. Predicted side-effect: a marked increase in her warmth toward Reed for roughly six months, as the contested-godfathership resolves and her unconscious frees up emotional bandwidth she did not know was occupied. She herself will not articulate this. Sue may notice.

**GIVEN:** Doom is restored after a defeat, *because of her quiet intervention.*
**EXPECT:** This is the historically documented pattern (FF #1-era restoration of his intellect). She will repeat it under sufficient strategic justification. The prediction is that the threshold for repeating it gets *lower* each time it succeeds — a slow normalization curve. Auditors should treat this as the highest-leverage habit-formation risk in her behavioral file.

---

## 3. The Wound-Touching Conditions

The subject's specific wounds, derived from §§1–3 of the master workup, and the predicted responses to their being touched.

**GIVEN:** Someone — an adult, a peer, a hostile — speaks to her *as a child,* condescends, talks past her, pats her head, calls her "sweetheart" in a context where she has just demonstrated competence.
**EXPECT:** Visible micro-response: a single beat of stillness, eyes narrowing fractionally, then a precise verbal correction delivered at slightly lower volume than her prior register (her contempt-tell — she goes quieter, not louder). She will not let it go quickly; the person will be subtly cut out of subsequent information flows for the rest of the engagement, sometimes for the rest of the relationship. The intensity is disproportionate to the offense, which is the diagnostic feature: this is identity-work, not etiquette.

**GIVEN:** She is told — by Reed, by an adversary, by a sufficiently authoritative voice — that her existence is owed to Doom, that she is in some sense his.
**EXPECT:** No visible reaction in the moment. Internally: this is the deepest natal wound and she has had to metabolize it since toddlerhood. She has a prepared cognitive defense: *I am owed to no one; the transaction was between my parents and him; I am the consequence, not the consideration.* She will deploy this defense to herself, not aloud. Where it becomes observable: in the subsequent 48–72 hours she will engage in some small but pointed act of autonomy — a unilateral decision, a refused instruction, a private project escalated. She is reasserting authorship over herself, quietly.

**GIVEN:** Reed makes a major decision badly — emotionally, paternally, or strategically — and she sees it in real time.
**EXPECT:** She will not correct him publicly. She will correct him privately, often within hours, in measured language. If he does not adjust, she will route around him. The wound here is older than the moment: every instance of Reed-insufficiency confirms her parentified-self's reason for existing, which is gratifying *and* exhausting *and* sad. Predicted long-term tell: she experiences a complicated affective response to her father's *successes,* which can momentarily look like coolness or under-celebration. She is not jealous; she is, briefly, unemployed.

**GIVEN:** Discovery that she has been wrong about a major model — a misread of an adversary, a miscalculation that cost something.
**EXPECT:** Acute private distress disproportionate to the actual cost, because her self-concept is organized around accurate modeling. Observable: withdrawal for 24–72 hours into a workspace, refusal of meals at standard times, abrupt termination of conversations she would normally engage. Recovery pattern: she rebuilds the failed model in writing, explicitly, and shares the rebuild with one trusted figure (historically Sue, occasionally Doom in the apprenticeship period, increasingly a peer as she ages). This is one of her healthiest reflexes and a strong long-term prognosis indicator.

**GIVEN:** Someone she has been quietly managing — a parent, a sibling, a teammate — discovers the management and confronts her with it.
**EXPECT:** The hardest scenario for her, harder than direct combat. Her covert-action habit is her largest unaddressed liability and she knows it. Predicted response: initial attempt at justification on outcome grounds (*you are alive / safe / successful because of what I did*), which she will recognize mid-sentence as inadequate. If the confronter holds firm, she will eventually concede — but she will concede *the specific instance* and try to preserve the general pattern. Real reform requires the confrontation to come from Sue and to be sustained.
